STATISTICALAPPEI\DIX

Definitions and Explanatory Notes

The following general notes supplement the footnotes given below the individual tables:

l. In an attempt to bring the material up-to-date provisional figures are included in some tables.

Z. Figures in some tables have been rounded off to the nearest final digit. Hence there may be a slight

discrepancy between the total as shown and the sum of its components.

3. Differences as compared with previously published figures are due to subsequent revisions.

4. Values indicated within parenthesis are negative values.

5. The following symbols have been used throughout:-

n.a. = not available

= nil

= negligible

WEIGHTS AND MEASURES

Conversion Factors

British to Metric Units

I acre = 0.405 hectares (ha)I pound (lb) = 0.454 kilogrammes (kg.)I long ton (2240 lbs) = 1.016 metric tons (Mt. Ton)I hundred weight (cwt) = 50.802 kg.

I mile = 1.609 kilometres (km.)I long ton mile = 1.635 Mt. Ton km.I lb/acre = l.l2l kg./ha

1 cwt/acre = L25.536 kg./ha

I pint = 0.75 litresI imperial gallon = 4.55 litres

Metric to British Units

I hectare = 2.47 L acres

I kilogramme = 2.205lbsI Mt. Ton (1,000 kg.) = 0.984long ton

I metre = 3.281 feet

I kilometre = 0.621 mileI Mt. Ton kilometre = 0.6l2long ton mileI litre = 1.76 pints -0.219 imp. gallons

1 kg./ha = 0.8gZ lb/acre

Paddy/Rice Conversions

I bushel of paddy (46 lbs) = 20.87 kg.

I Mt. Ton paddy = 47.92 bushels paddy= 0.7 Mt. Ton rice

I Mt. Ton rice = 68.46 bushels paddy= 1.43 Mt. Ton paddy

I bushel paddy/acre = 51.55 kg. paddy/ha

Wage Rate Index Numbers

The Index numbers are calculated on fixed weights based on the numbers employed as at 31December1978. The wage rates used in the calculation ol lndex Numbers are minimumwages for diflerent trades tixed by the Wages Boards.The Index lor Central Government employees has been revised based on the number olemployees and total salaries as at 1 January 1986. The wage rates used in the calculation ollndex Numbers are the initial salaries and wages in each respective Ecale.The Index refers to wage rates ot tea growing and manufacturing, rubber growing andmanuf acturing, coconut, cocoa, cardamoms, and pepper growing lrades only.Including baking, brick and tile manulacturing, coconut manufacluring, prinling, textile, tyre

and tube manulacturing, coir mattresses and bristle f ibre export, hosierymanufacturing, engineering, garment manufacturing, match manufac-turing, biscuit and confectionary, tea export and rubber export tradesonly.This includes cinema, molor transport and nursing home trades only.Combined index tor workers in agriculture, in industry & commerce andIn servtces,A combined index for Non-Executive OJticers and Minor Employees.NWRI = Nominal Wage Rate Index RWRI = Real Wage Rate IndexProvisional

(a) This new monetary survey is based on ihe aggregate data peltaining to both Domestic Banking Units(DBUs) and Foreign Currency Banking Units (FCBUs) of banks operaling in Sri Lanka.Definitional changes have been adopted in aggregating DBUs and FCBUs dala to avoid double countingand misclassification of assets and liabilities. The maior changes ar€:(1) All DBU placements in FCBUs are recorded as domestic assets, while all DBU borrowings f rom FCBUsare recorded as domestic liabilities.(2)'Foreign currency deposits of DBUs are classified on the basis of ownership ratherthan on the basis ofcurrency. Hence, the following apply:(i) One hall (50 per cent) of NRFC deposits are treated as domestic deposit liabilities;(ii) All RNNFC balances are treated as foreign liabilities;

(Contd.)

(iii) All other domestic foreign currency accounts are lreated as domestic depositliabilities.(b) External assets (net) of the Central Bank and commercial banks (including outward bills).(c) Currency and demand deposits ot the public.(d) Time and savings deposits of the public held with commercial banks.

1 ,010,5201,017,8241,040,3431,062,1761 ,086,3301,098,209(a) This financial survey is based on the aggregate data pertaining to Domestic Banking Units (DBUs)and Foreign Currency Banking Units (FCBUs) of commercial banks, Licenced Specilised Banks(LSBs) and Finance Companies (FtNCOs) operating in Sri Lanka.Definitional changes have been adopted in aggregating DBU, FCBUs, LSBs and FINCOS data toavoid double counting and misclassification of assels and liabilities. The major changes are:(1) All DBU placements in FCBUs are recorded as domestic assets, while all DBU borrowingsf rom FCBUs are recorded as domestic liabilities.(2, Foreign currency deposits of DBUs are classilied on the basis of ownership rather than on thebasis of currency. Hence, the f ollowing apply:(i) One half (50 percent) of NRFC deposits are treated as domestic deoosit liabilities:

Source: Central Bank of Sri Lanka(ii) All RNNFC balances are treated as loreign liabilities;(iii) All other domestic f oreign currency accounts are treated as domestic liabilities.(b) External assets (nel) ol the Central Bank, Commercial banks (including outward bills), LSBs and FINGOS .(c) Currency,demanddepositsandquasi-moneyinDBUsinthistablediflerfromthoseinTablell9duetothefactthat LSBs and FINCOs are not treated as public under lhis broad monetary survey (Mo) definition.(d) Time and savings deposits of the public with commercial banks and LSBs and FlNCOs.(e) Credit extended by the Monetary Authority, DBUs, FCBUS, LSBs and FINCOs to the Government, net ofGovernment deposits with banks and Governmenl cash deposits.(l) Provisional
